< username>
CraftyFrogger<//username>
< Review>
I go here for Magic. It is open most days of the week. It is closed on Tuesdays. I usually am playing or buying cards. They have a huge selection of cards to buy from. You can call and ask if they have certain cards and it can placed on hold for you. The place operates cash only. The card are usually $0.25 and up. They sell some food if you get hungry while you are in a tournament. They have draft, commander and standard tournaments; sometimes it happens only on some days or there are not enough people, so it might be best to call in advance. The players are always changing, but some of the reoccurring players can be a bit more competitive than others.
I know that at this location there are Yu-gi-oh events and Dungeons and Dragons. I do not think the people at this shop do either of those, but there is adjacent shops within the same area.
There are bathrooms available. The women's restroom is always locked, so you need to ask for the key. It's a nice place. The workers are very nice and accommodating.<//Review>

Every format you can think of is played here on a regular basis. <user>115762725320313826317<//user>< username>
Ron McCabe</username>
< Date>
1393471056542</Date>
< Rating>
5</Rating>
< review>
I have seen been to many food banks across the country.  This is one of the best organized ones I have seen. I was particularly impressed with their efficient distribution of the food they receive to the pantries and people that need it.

Most of the food banks I have seen drone on and on about how large their warehouse is to store all their food.Feeding America San Diego has a totally different approach. They understand that rapidly and efficiently distributing the food they receive is their main purpose. They are the only food bank in America that I have toured that is actually considering moving to a smaller space. They would use this savings to provide better services  to the pantries they serve. I smile every time I think of their operation.</review>

< username>
Dean Martens</username>
< text>
I've been volunteering at Feeding San Diego at least weekly for nearly six years.  What keeps me going back week after week?  A sense of purpose, the feeling of accomplishment and appreciation.  All the projects that get done by volunteers help SO many different people who are food insecure in the county.  Many shifts involve gleaning produce for the many different programs that FSD serves.  Processing food donations from food drives and store donations is also a big part of the what FSD does.  There are a lot of different tasks that need to get done all year round that requires lots of volunteers to keep costs down.  Because of volunteers, FSD monetary donations provide 4 meals for every dollar.  Plus there's a lot of fine people who work and volunteer there. If you want to make a difference in your community helping many people like military families, seniors, kids, and other families who don't have enough to afford all the essentials in their life (1 out of 8 in San Diego), this is the place to spend some of your time at.</text>
